season</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Pacific_typhoon_climatology" title="Pacific typhoon climatology">Pacific typhoon seasons</a><br/>\n<a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2004 Pacific typhoon season">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2005 Pacific typhoon season">2005</a>, <b>2006</b>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2007 Pacific typhoon season">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2008 Pacific typhoon season">2008</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <b>2006 Pacific typhoon season</b> was a near-average season that produced a total of 23 named storms, 15 typhoons, and six super typhoons. The season ran throughout 2006, though most tropical cyclones typically <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">develop</a> between May and October. The season\'s first named storm, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chanchu" title="Typhoon Chanchu">Chanchu</a>, developed on May 9, while the season\'s last named storm, Trami, dissipated on December 20. This season was also much active, costly and deadly than the <a href="/wiki/2005_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2005 Pacific typhoon season">previous season</a>.</p>\n<p>Throughout the season, many typhoons made landfall at a higher intensity. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Saomai" title="Typhoon Saomai">Typhoon Saomai</a> was the most powerful typhoon to strike <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> for over 50 years, as a Category 4 typhoon, responsible for over 400 deaths. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Shanshan_(2006)" title="Typhoon Shanshan (2006)">Typhoon Shanshan</a> struck <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and became the costliest typhoon this season with a total damage of about $2.5 billion. The <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> got hit by a total of six typhoons, which saw the highest number since <a href="/wiki/1974_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1974 Pacific typhoon season">1974</a>. All six typhoons were responsible for over 1,000 casualties and several millions of damages. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Ioke" title="Typhoon Ioke">Typhoon Ioke</a>, which formed from the <a href="/wiki/2006_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2006 Pacific hurricane season">Central Pacific</a>, entered the basin and became the strongest Central Pacific hurricane. Moreover, it was stated that the ratio of intense typhoons was 0.73, which was the highest since <a href="/wiki/1970_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1970 Pacific typhoon season">1970</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR2006_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSR2006-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The scope of this article is limited to the Pacific Ocean to the north of the equator between <a href="/wiki/100th_meridian_east" title="100th meridian east">100\xc2\xb0E</a> and <a href="/wiki/180th_meridian" title="180th meridian">180th meridian</a>. Within the northwestern Pacific Ocean, there are two separate agencies that assign names to tropical cyclones which can often result in a cyclone having two names. The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a>\xc2\xa0<small>(JMA)</small> will name a tropical cyclone should it be judged to have 10-minute <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">sustained wind speeds</a> of at least 65\xc2\xa0km/h (40\xc2\xa0mph) anywhere in the basin, whilst the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a>\xc2\xa0<small>(PAGASA)</small> assigns names to tropical cyclones which move into or form as a tropical depression in their area of responsibility located between 135\xc2\xb0E and 115\xc2\xb0E and between 5\xc2\xb0N\xe2\x80\x9325\xc2\xb0N regardless of whether or not a tropical cyclone has already been given a name by the JMA. Tropical depressions that are monitored by the United States\' <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a>\xc2\xa0<small>(JTWC)</small> are given a number with a "W" suffix.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" <small>(bottom-right)</small>, active on August 7</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_forecasts">Seasonal forecasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Seasonal forecasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right">\n<tr>\n<th>TSR forecasts<br/>\nDate</th>\n<th>Tropical<br/>\nstorms</th>\n<th>Total<br/>\nTyphoons</th>\n<th>Intense<br/>\nTCs</th>\n<th>ACE</th>\n<th>Ref</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><small>Average (1965\xe2\x80\x932005)</small></td>\n<td>26.7</td>\n<td>16.9</td>\n<td>8.6</td>\n<td>305</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_May_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_May-2">[2]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>March 7, 2006</td>\n<td>27.1</td>\n<td>17.1</td>\n<td>8.4</td>\n<td>298</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_March_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_March-3">[3]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>May 5, 2006</td>\n<td>29.0</td>\n<td>18.6</td>\n<td>9.2</td>\n<td>326</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_May_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_May-2">[2]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>June 7, 2006</td>\n<td>29.0</td>\n<td>18.6</td>\n<td>9.0</td>\n<td>315</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_Jun_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_Jun-4">[4]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>July 5, 2006</td>\n<td>29.0</td>\n<td>18.6</td>\n<td>10.0</td>\n<td>349</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_Jul_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_Jul-5">[5]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>August 4, 2006</td>\n<td>29.0</td>\n<td>18.6</td>\n<td>9.3</td>\n<td>325</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_Aug_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_Aug-6">[6]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th></th>\n<th>Forecast<br/>\nCenter</th>\n<th>Tropical<br/>\ncyclones</th>\n<th>Tropical<br/>\nstorms</th>\n<th>Typhoons</th>\n<th>Ref</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Actual activity</b>:</td>\n<td>JMA</td>\n<td>39</td>\n<td>23</td>\n<td>15</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Actual activity</b>:</td>\n<td>JTWC</td>\n<td>28</td>\n<td>23</td>\n<td>15</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Actual activity</b>:</td>\n<td>PAGASA</td>\n<td>20</td>\n<td>16</td>\n<td>10</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>During the year several national meteorological services and scientific agencies forecast how many tropical cyclones, tropical storms, and typhoons will form during a season and/or how many tropical cyclones will affect a particular country. These agencies included the Tropical Storm Risk\xc2\xa0<small>(TSR)</small> Consortium of <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, <a href="/wiki/PAGASA" title="PAGASA">PAGASA</a> and Taiwan\'s <a href="/wiki/Central_Weather_Bureau" title="Central Weather Bureau">Central Weather Bureau</a>. Some of the forecasts took into consideration what happened in previous seasons and the La Ni\xc3\xb1a conditions that were observed during the previous year.</p>\n<p>On March 7, Tropical Storm Risk issued its first forecast for the season at an extended-range, forecasting a close to average season of 27 tropical storms, 17 typhoons and 8 intense typhoons. The ACE predicted was around 298.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_March_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_March-3">[3]</a></sup> By May 5, Tropical Storm Risk issued their second forecast for the season, raising their numbers to 29 tropical storms, 19 typhoons and 9 intense typhoons, with an ACE of 326. This is due to the observed warming of sea-surface temperatures in the Ni\xc3\xb1o 3.75 region and current patterns within the Central Pacific, indicating slightly higher activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_May_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_May-2">[2]</a></sup> TSR released its third forecast for the season on June 7, predicting the same numbers with the same reason. Though on their fourth forecast during July 5, TSR stated that the 2006 season will be 15% above the 1965\xe2\x80\x932005 norm. Therefore, they raised the number of intense typhoons to 10, and their ACE to 349. The other reason behind this is due to the fact that there was an increase in tropical activity and much warmer SSTs over in the Ni\xc3\xb1o 3.75 region than the previous forecast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_Jul_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_Jul-5">[5]</a></sup> On August 4, TSR released their final forecast. They reduced the number of intense typhoons to 9, and the ACE to 325. This was because it was reported that a slight decrease in tropical activity from the previous forecast and is due solely of a slight decrease in SSTs over in the same region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR_Aug_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR_Aug-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_Summary">Seasonal Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Seasonal Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<center>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_255d0e9d02361654ff25bd138ab2efc4"></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/255d0e9d02361654ff25bd138ab2efc4.png" usemap="#timeline_255d0e9d02361654ff25bd138ab2efc4"/></div>\n</center>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png/350px-Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png/525px-Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png/700px-Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png 2x" width="350"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Late_2006_Philippine_typhoon_tracks.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTracks of typhoons that affected the Philippines during late 2006</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Pacific typhoon season runs throughout 2006 and has no official bounds, though most tropical cyclones from this basin generally develops from the months from May through to October. Despite the season turned out to be active, most tropical cyclones developed during the second half of the year, with only one typhoon, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chanchu" title="Typhoon Chanchu">Chanchu</a> developing during the month of May. Some minor systems also developed before May, with the first tropical system of the year, Agaton, developing to the east of <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> on January 20, bringing minor damages as it crossed the country few days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan06_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jan06-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">Tropical cyclogenesis</a> had become much favorable during late June with formations of Jelawat and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Ewiniar_(2006)" title="Typhoon Ewiniar (2006)">Ewiniar</a>. It was also during the same time when NOAA had stated that the weak 2006\xe2\x80\x9307 El Ni\xc3\xb1o had started.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> From mid July to early August, three "back-to-back" storms made landfall over in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, which were <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bilis" title="Tropical Storm Bilis">Bilis</a>, Kaemi and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Prapiroon_(2006)" title="Typhoon Prapiroon (2006)">Prapiroon</a>. With all three combined, more than 900 people have been dead and damages were reported more than US$5 billion. Shortly thereafter, environments throughout most of the basin became favorable with less shear, more convection and warmer water, as three simultaneous storms, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Maria_(2006)" title="Typhoon Maria (2006)">Maria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Saomai" title="Typhoon Saomai">Saomai</a> and Bopha, formed and affected three different landmasses such as <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, China and Taiwan, respectively. Later in the same month, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a> had entered the basin from the Central Pacific as the strongest Central Pacific storm in recorder history, as a Category 5 powerful storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aug06_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aug06-9">[9]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On September, an unnamed and unclassified tropical storm have been discovered by meteorologist Gary Padgett and Dr. Karl Hoarau. Later, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Xangsane" title="Typhoon Xangsane">Typhoon Xangsane</a> affected <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, causing major damages with more than 200 people dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oct06_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oct06-10">[10]</a></sup> The country saw four storms making landfall, with three of them reaching Category 4 or 5 super typhoon status. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Cimaron_(2006)" title="Typhoon Cimaron (2006)">Typhoon Cimaron</a> made landfall over in northern Luzon as a Category 5 super typhoon with minimal damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Summary_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Summary-11">[11]</a></sup> By November, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chebi" title="Typhoon Chebi">Typhoon Chebi</a> made landfall in the same area as Cimaron, though effects from the typhoon were much smaller than Cimaron. Although by late November, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Durian" title="Typhoon Durian">Typhoon Durian</a> made landfall in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicol_region" title="Bicol region">Bicol region</a>. Combined effects with ash from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayon_Volcano" title="Mayon Volcano">Mayon Volcano</a> had killed over 1,500 people and damgaes at least US$530 million. Durian also crossed the basin and into the <a href="/wiki/2006_North_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season" title="2006 North Indian Ocean cyclone season">North Indian Ocean basin</a>, the first time since <a href="/wiki/2003_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2003 Pacific typhoon season">2003</a>. During early December, two systems formed. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Utor_(2006)" title="Typhoon Utor (2006)">Typhoon Utor</a> crossed <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a> with minimal damage; and Tropical Storm Trami, a very weak system that didn\'t affect any landmasses became the final tropical cyclone and dissipated on December 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSR2006_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSR2006-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Agaton">Tropical Depression Agaton</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Agaton">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Tropical_Depression_Agaton_2006.JPG/300px-Tropical_Depression_Agaton_2006.JPG 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agaton_(PAGASA)_2006_track.png"><img alt="Agaton (PAGASA) 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Agaton_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png/300px-Agaton_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>January 20\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 January 27</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>55\xc2\xa0km/h (35\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On January 20, the JMA began monitoring a minor tropical depression located about 555\xc2\xa0km (345\xc2\xa0mi) east of <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a> in the southern Philippines. As it traveled in an erratic northwestward direction, it slowly became better organized. On January 23, the JMA assessed the storm to have attained winds of 55\xc2\xa0km/h (35\xc2\xa0mph <small>10-minute winds</small>). Around the same time, PAGASA began issuing advisories on the system and gave it the local name <i>Agaton</i>. The depression weakened as it crossed over northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samar_Island" title="Samar Island">Samar Island</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>. Traveling towards the west, the system failed to strengthen and dissipated on January 27 while located over the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, about halfway between <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPJanuary_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPJanuary-12">[12]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Tropical_Depression_01W_(Basyang)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_01W_.28Basyang.29">Tropical Depression 01W (Basyang)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 01W (Basyang)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2006_TS01W_peak.jpg"><img alt="2006 TS01W peak.jpg" data-file-height="3205" data-file-width="3611" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/2006_TS01W_peak.jpg/150px-2006_TS01W_peak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/2006_TS01W_peak.jpg/225px-2006_TS01W_peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/2006_TS01W_peak.jpg/300px-2006_TS01W_peak.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1-W_2006_track.png"><img alt="1-W 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/1-W_2006_track.png/150px-1-W_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/1-W_2006_track.png/225px-1-W_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/1-W_2006_track.png/300px-1-W_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>March 3\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 March 7</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>55\xc2\xa0km/h (35\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1004\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On March 4, a tropical depression formed out of a wave close to the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> southeast of <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">JTWC</a> upgraded it to Tropical Storm 01W at 3\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> the same day. The JTWC downgraded it back to a depression on March 5 due to shear, and it never regained tropical storm strength before dissipating on March 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrl_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrl-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Chanchu_(Caloy)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Chanchu_.28Caloy.29">Typhoon Chanchu (Caloy)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Typhoon Chanchu (Caloy)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Chanchu16-05-06.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Chanchu16-05-06.jpg" data-file-height="9400" data-file-width="7200" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Typhoon_Chanchu16-05-06.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Chanchu16-05-06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Typhoon_Chanchu16-05-06.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Chanchu16-05-06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Typhoon_Chanchu16-05-06.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Chanchu16-05-06.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chanchu_2006_track.png"><img alt="Chanchu 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1547" data-file-width="2000" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chanchu_2006_track.png/150px-Chanchu_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chanchu_2006_track.png/225px-Chanchu_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chanchu_2006_track.png/300px-Chanchu_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>May 8\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 May 18</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>175\xc2\xa0km/h (110\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 930\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chanchu" title="Typhoon Chanchu">Typhoon Chanchu</a></div>\n<p>On May 8, the JMA started to track a tropical depression about 175\xc2\xa0km (110\xc2\xa0mi) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, and later the JTWC followed suit giving the designation of <i>02W</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May06_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-May06-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jma2006_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-jma2006-15">[15]</a></sup> By the next day, 02W had intensified into a tropical storm, with the JMA naming it <i>Chanchu</i>. The PAGASA had also declared that Chanchu had entered their area, giving the local name <i>Caloy</i>. Chanchu reached typhoon intensity and made its first landfall over in <a href="/wiki/Samar" title="Samar">Samar</a> on May 11, and several hours later, it struck <a href="/wiki/Mindoro" title="Mindoro">Mindoro</a> at Category 2 typhoon intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May06_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-May06-14">[14]</a></sup> As Chanchu emerged to the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, and moved northward, the storm explosively intensified into a Category 4 typhoon and reached peak intensity with 10-minute sustained winds of 175\xc2\xa0km/h (110\xc2\xa0mph) on May 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May06_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-May06-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jma2006_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-jma2006-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T0601BT_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-T0601BT-16">[16]</a></sup> By May 17, Chanchu rapidly weakened into a severe tropical storm as it made its landfall over in <a href="/wiki/Shantou" title="Shantou">Shantou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guandong</a>. Both the JMA and the JTWC issued its final advisory on May 18 as it became extratropical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May06_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-May06-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jma2006_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-jma2006-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-T0601BT_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-T0601BT-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, the storm caused 41 deaths and a total of <a href="/wiki/Philippine_peso" title="Philippine peso">\xe2\x82\xb1</a>117.6 million (US$2.15 million) in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-17">[17]</a></sup> Despite Chanchu didn\'t made landfall over in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, several ships sunk and lost. A total of 18 people, who are fishermen, were dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reut520_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-reut520-18">[18]</a></sup> Chanchu is also the most intense typhoon on <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a>\'s record to enter the South China Sea in May. Chanchu necessitated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Tropical_Cyclone_Warning_Signals" title="Hong Kong Tropical Cyclone Warning Signals">Strong Wind Signal no. 3</a> in both Hong Kong and Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hko_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-hko-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smg_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-smg-20">[20]</a></sup> In Hong Kong, the Gale force signal 8 should have been hoisted for at least 10 hours as sustained gales were affecting the Eastern part of the territory, where the hourly mean wind reached 83\xc2\xa0km/h, with gust reaching over 100\xc2\xa0km/h in some areas. Overall damage in China was at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" title="Chinese yuan">\xc2\xa5</a>7 billion (US$872 million).</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Tropical_Storm_Jelawat_(Domeng)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Jelawat_.28Domeng.29">Tropical Storm Jelawat (Domeng)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Jelawat (Domeng)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:03W_Jelawat_28_jun_2006_0030Z.jpg"><img alt="03W Jelawat 28 jun 2006 0030Z.jpg" data-file-height="898" data-file-width="898" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/03W_Jelawat_28_jun_2006_0030Z.jpg/150px-03W_Jelawat_28_jun_2006_0030Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/03W_Jelawat_28_jun_2006_0030Z.jpg/225px-03W_Jelawat_28_jun_2006_0030Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/03W_Jelawat_28_jun_2006_0030Z.jpg/300px-03W_Jelawat_28_jun_2006_0030Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jelawat_2006_track.png"><img alt="Jelawat 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Jelawat_2006_track.png/150px-Jelawat_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Jelawat_2006_track.png/225px-Jelawat_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Jelawat_2006_track.png/300px-Jelawat_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>June 24\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 June 29</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>75\xc2\xa0km/h (45\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 996\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On June 24, the JMA started to track a weak tropical depression located to the southeast of <a href="/wiki/Samar" title="Samar">Samar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jma2006_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-jma2006-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> After crossing the archipelago, as it emerged to the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> on June 26, the PAGASA named it <i>Domeng</i> while the JTWC had started issuing advisories with the designation of <i>03W</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-03WBT_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-03WBT-22">[22]</a></sup> Moving northwestward, 03W had entered in an area of favorable environments and intensified into a tropical storm, with the naming of <i>Jelawat</i> on June 27. Jelawat made landfall over Southern China and fully dissipated inland on June 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jma2006_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-jma2006-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-03WBT_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-03WBT-22">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The storm dropped heavy rainfall across southern China and <a href="/wiki/Haikou" title="Haikou">Haikou</a> recorded a rainfall of 309.7\xc2\xa0mm (12\xc2\xa0inches) during the storm passage. A total of 8.6\xc2\xa0inches (220\xc2\xa0mm) rain fell in 16 hours in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kampung_Bundu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kampung Bundu (page does not exist)">Kampung Bundu</a>, Malaysia. The rainfall killed seven people and left one missing. The flooding from Jelawat ruined 200 square kilometres of farmland and destroyed 190 houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shanghaidaily_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-shanghaidaily-23">[23]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Ewiniar_(Ester)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Ewiniar_.28Ester.29">Typhoon Ewiniar (Ester)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Typhoon Ewiniar (Ester)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0super\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Ewiniar_07_july_2006_0210Z.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Ewiniar 07 july 2006 0210Z.jpg" data-file-height="8400" data-file-width="6400" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Typhoon_Ewiniar_07_july_2006_0210Z.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Ewiniar_07_july_2006_0210Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Typhoon_Ewiniar_07_july_2006_0210Z.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Ewiniar_07_july_2006_0210Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Typhoon_Ewiniar_07_july_2006_0210Z.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Ewiniar_07_july_2006_0210Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ewiniar_2006_track.png"><img alt="Ewiniar 2006 track.png" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Ewiniar_2006_track.png/150px-Ewiniar_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Ewiniar_2006_track.png/225px-Ewiniar_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Ewiniar_2006_track.png/300px-Ewiniar_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>June 29\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 10</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>185\xc2\xa0km/h (115\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 930\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Ewiniar_(2006)" title="Typhoon Ewiniar (2006)">Typhoon Ewiniar (2006)</a></div>\n<p>On June 29, a persistent tropical disturbance was classified as a tropical depression by the JTWC while east of <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>. The depression moved northwestward and was upgraded to Tropical Storm 04W by the JTWC on June 30. The JMA designated the storm Tropical Storm Ewiniar at around the same time. The name "Ewiniar" was submitted by the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a>, and refers to a traditional storm god of <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">Chuuk</a>.</p>\n<p>Ewiniar was responsible for at least 30 deaths in China, which it brushed as a typhoon. The typhoon gradually weakened as it moved over colder waters, and made landfall in South Korea on July 10 as a severe tropical storm. As Ewiniar moved across the country, it passed within 30 miles (48\xc2\xa0km) of <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>. The storm brought heavy rain that triggered floods and mudslides in the southern part of the country, killing at least six people. Ewiniar became extratropical over the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a> on the same day.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Bilis_(Florita)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Bilis_.28Florita.29">Severe Tropical Storm Bilis (Florita)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Bilis (Florita)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Bilis_2006_peak.jpg"><img alt="TS Bilis 2006 peak.jpg" data-file-height="1120" data-file-width="1220" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/TS_Bilis_2006_peak.jpg/150px-TS_Bilis_2006_peak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/TS_Bilis_2006_peak.jpg/225px-TS_Bilis_2006_peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/TS_Bilis_2006_peak.jpg/300px-TS_Bilis_2006_peak.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bilis_2006_track.png"><img alt="Bilis 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1298" data-file-width="2000" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Bilis_2006_track.png/150px-Bilis_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Bilis_2006_track.png/225px-Bilis_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Bilis_2006_track.png/300px-Bilis_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 8\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 16</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>110\xc2\xa0km/h (70\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 970\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bilis" title="Tropical Storm Bilis">Tropical Storm Bilis</a></div>\n<p>A tropical disturbance northeast of <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">Yap</a> developed sufficient convection to be designated a tropical depression on July 8. The depression strengthened into a tropical storm the next day, and was designated Tropical Storm Bilis by the JMA. The word "Bilis", submitted by the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, means speed or swiftness. PAGASA operationally treated this storm as a typhoon for a short time on July 13, but it officially remained a tropical storm as it moved west-northwestward toward <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. After moving over northern Taiwan, Bilis made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>, China at 12:50\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Standard_Time" title="Chinese Standard Time">CST</a> on July 14, weakening into a tropical depression inland the next day. JMA carried the system as a tropical depression until July 17. Bilis brought very heavy rain, widespread flooding, landslides, and strong winds to the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, Taiwan and areas of mainland China, causing 672 deaths and $4.4\xc2\xa0billion (2006 US$) in damage.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Kaemi_(Glenda)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Kaemi_.28Glenda.29">Typhoon Kaemi (Glenda)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Typhoon Kaemi (Glenda)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:06W-Kaemi.jpg"><img alt="06W-Kaemi.jpg" data-file-height="898" data-file-width="898" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/06W-Kaemi.jpg/150px-06W-Kaemi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/06W-Kaemi.jpg/225px-06W-Kaemi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/06W-Kaemi.jpg/300px-06W-Kaemi.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaemi_2006_track.png"><img alt="Kaemi 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Kaemi_2006_track.png/150px-Kaemi_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Kaemi_2006_track.png/225px-Kaemi_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Kaemi_2006_track.png/300px-Kaemi_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 17\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 27</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>150\xc2\xa0km/h (90\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 960\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical depression formed on July 18 near the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a>, it quickly strengthened to tropical storm strength the same day. On July 19, the storm was named Kaemi by the JMA. The correct name Gaemi was submitted by South Korea and is a Korean word for <a href="/wiki/Ant" title="Ant">ant</a>. It strengthened into a severe tropical storm on July 20, and further deepened into a typhoon 24 hours later. Kaemi made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Jinjiang,_Fujian" title="Jinjiang, Fujian">Jinjiang</a>, Fujian at 3:50\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Standard_Time" title="Chinese Standard Time">CST</a> on July 25 as a minimal typhoon.</p>\n<p>Heavy rainfall in Taiwan caused flooding and four minor injuries. Rain also fell heavily in the northern Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trmm_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-trmm-24">[24]</a></sup> The storm has also killed at least 32\xc2\xa0people in China, while another 60\xc2\xa0people are missing. Agricultural losses in Taiwan amounted to NT$73\xc2\xa0million (US$2.2\xc2\xa0million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Total damages from the storm amounted to $450\xc2\xa0million.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Prapiroon_(Henry)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Prapiroon_.28Henry.29">Typhoon Prapiroon (Henry)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Typhoon Prapiroon (Henry)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Prapiroon_02_aug_2006_0550Z.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Prapiroon 02 aug 2006 0550Z.jpg" data-file-height="9000" data-file-width="7200" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Typhoon_Prapiroon_02_aug_2006_0550Z.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Prapiroon_02_aug_2006_0550Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Typhoon_Prapiroon_02_aug_2006_0550Z.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Prapiroon_02_aug_2006_0550Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Typhoon_Prapiroon_02_aug_2006_0550Z.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Prapiroon_02_aug_2006_0550Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prapiroon_2006_track.png"><img alt="Prapiroon 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Prapiroon_2006_track.png/150px-Prapiroon_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Prapiroon_2006_track.png/225px-Prapiroon_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Prapiroon_2006_track.png/300px-Prapiroon_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 27\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 5</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>120\xc2\xa0km/h (75\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 970\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Prapiroon_(2006)" title="Typhoon Prapiroon (2006)">Typhoon Prapiroon (2006)</a></div>\n<p>PAGASA named a system east of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> as Tropical Depression Henry later on the same day that the JMA recognised it as a tropical depression on July 27. The JTWC upgraded this system to a tropical storm on the morning of August 1. <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> also did so and issued the Tropical Cyclone Signal No. 1 that same afternoon, and shortly after the JMA upgraded the system to Tropical Storm Prapiroon. The name Prapiroon was submitted by <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and is the name of a Thai rain deity. The JMA upgraded the storm to a severe tropical storm on the morning of August 2. PAGASA ceased advisories on the storm shortly after as it moved out of its area of responsibility. The JTWC and the HKO upgraded Prapiroon to a typhoon at 3\xc2\xa0a.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>, while the JMA officially upgraded it to a typhoon at 12\xc2\xa0p.m. UTC (8\xc2\xa0p.m. <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Time" title="Hong Kong Time">HKT</a>). Prapiroon necessitated the first Tropical Cyclone Signal No. 8 in Macau this year. In Hong Kong, the flag raising ceremony at the Golden Bauhinia Square was cancelled due to strong wind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Prapiroon made landfall at 7:20\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Standard_Time" title="Chinese Standard Time">CST</a> on August 3.</p>\n<p>The strong winds due to the storm resulted in 70% of flights being cancelled, delayed or diverted in the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_International_Airport" title="Hong Kong International Airport">Hong Kong International Airport</a>, the highest since the opening in 1999. However, the airport remained open throughout the storm passage and many flights successfully landed or took off on August 3. Inbound flights were rerouted to nearby airports and outbound flights were cancelled or postponed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> On landfall in <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> province, China, it forced the evacuation of some 660,000\xc2\xa0people and caused an estimated 5.4\xc2\xa0billion Chinese yuan worth of damage. 77\xc2\xa0people were reported killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> It also affected <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a>, Guangxi and <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a>. Prapiroon degenerated into an area of low pressure on August 6.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Maria">Typhoon Maria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Typhoon Maria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_maria_2006.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon maria 2006.jpg" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="2800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Typhoon_maria_2006.jpg/150px-Typhoon_maria_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Typhoon_maria_2006.jpg/225px-Typhoon_maria_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Typhoon_maria_2006.jpg/300px-Typhoon_maria_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maria_2006_track.png"><img alt="Maria 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1662" data-file-width="2000" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Maria_2006_track.png/150px-Maria_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Maria_2006_track.png/225px-Maria_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Maria_2006_track.png/300px-Maria_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 3\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 10</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>130\xc2\xa0km/h (80\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 975\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Maria_(2006)" title="Typhoon Maria (2006)">Typhoon Maria (2006)</a></div>\n<p>Maria formed out of a tropical depression over the open waters of the western Pacific Ocean. On August\xc2\xa05, the JMA classified the depression as a tropical storm while the JTWC kept it as a depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MariaJMA_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-MariaJMA-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCBT_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCBT-30">[30]</a></sup> The storm quickly strengthened into a typhoon the next day, reaching its peak intensity with winds of 130\xc2\xa0km/h (80\xc2\xa0mph) early on August\xc2\xa06. The storm gradually weakened as it began to recurve, causing it to parallel the southeastern coast of Japan. On August\xc2\xa09, Maria weakened into a tropical depression and later into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> before dissipating on August\xc2\xa015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MariaJMA_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-MariaJMA-29">[29]</a></sup> Maria had only minor effects in Japan, mainly heavy rains which were estimated to have peaked over 400\xc2\xa0mm (15.7\xc2\xa0in) on the <a href="/wiki/Izu_Peninsula" title="Izu Peninsula">Izu Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> One person was killed after being struck by lightning and six others were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPAug_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPAug-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Saomai_(Juan)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Saomai_.28Juan.29">Typhoon Saomai (Juan)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Typhoon Saomai (Juan)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5\xc2\xa0super\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Saomai_10_aug_2006_0505Z.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Saomai 10 aug 2006 0505Z.jpg" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="5600" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Typhoon_Saomai_10_aug_2006_0505Z.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Saomai_10_aug_2006_0505Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Typhoon_Saomai_10_aug_2006_0505Z.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Saomai_10_aug_2006_0505Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Typhoon_Saomai_10_aug_2006_0505Z.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Saomai_10_aug_2006_0505Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saomai_2006_track.png"><img alt="Saomai 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1383" data-file-width="2000" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Saomai_2006_track.png/150px-Saomai_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Saomai_2006_track.png/225px-Saomai_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Saomai_2006_track.png/300px-Saomai_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 5\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 11</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>195\xc2\xa0km/h (120\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 925\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Saomai" title="Typhoon Saomai">Typhoon Saomai</a></div>\n<p>The JTWC identified a tropical depression near the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a> late on August 4 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>. The JMA designated it as such at 12\xc2\xa0a.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> August 5. Nine hours later, the JTWC upgraded Tropical Depression 08W to a tropical storm, three hours before the JMA named it Saomai. The name is from the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a> "<a class="extiw" href="https://vi.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sao_Kim" title="vi:Sao Kim">sao Mai</a>", meaning "Morning Star",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> a reference to the planet <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a>.</p>\n<p>The JTWC designated it a typhoon at 3\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> August 6. The JMA upgraded Saomai to a Severe Tropical Storm at 6\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>, and as it continued to strengthen, it was upgraded to a typhoon just 12 hours later. Saomai passed into the Area of Responsibility of PAGASA on August 8 and was named Typhoon Juan by PAGASA. On August 8, the storm underwent explosive development, and by August 9 it had become a Category\xc2\xa05-equivalent super typhoon.</p>\n<p>Saomai made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang" title="Zhejiang">Zhejiang</a>, China on August 10 with maximum sustained winds of 115 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knots</a> (1-minute mean), stronger than Chanchu earlier this season. Saomai was responsible for at least 458 deaths, mostly in China, and $2.5\xc2\xa0billion (2006\xc2\xa0USD) in damage.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Bopha_(Inday)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Bopha_.28Inday.29">Severe Tropical Storm Bopha (Inday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Bopha (Inday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS_Bopha_2006.jpg"><img alt="STS Bopha 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="4800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/STS_Bopha_2006.jpg/150px-STS_Bopha_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/STS_Bopha_2006.jpg/225px-STS_Bopha_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/STS_Bopha_2006.jpg/300px-STS_Bopha_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bopha_2006_track.png"><img alt="Bopha 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bopha_2006_track.png/150px-Bopha_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bopha_2006_track.png/225px-Bopha_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bopha_2006_track.png/300px-Bopha_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 5\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 10</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>100\xc2\xa0km/h (65\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 980\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The JMA identified a tropical depression in the open Pacific on August 5. PAGASA named this storm late on August 5 as it was forecast to enhance the southwest <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> and bring rains to the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Around 1800\xc2\xa0UTC, the JTWC declared that the system had developed into a tropical depression and gave it the number 10W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCBT10W_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCBT10W-36">[36]</a></sup> JMA upgraded it to Tropical Storm Bopha on August 6. The name Bopha was submitted by <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> and is a flower and girls\' name. Around this time, the JTWC also upgraded the system to a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCBT10W_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCBT10W-36">[36]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The JTWC recognised its existence as a tropical depression at 9\xc2\xa0a.m. UTC the same day before upgrading it to a tropical storm at 3\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>. The JMA then upgraded it to a severe tropical storm as it slowly churned westwards at 12\xc2\xa0a.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> August 7 before downgrading it 18 hours later. Bopha unexpectedly restrengthened into a severe tropical storm at 3\xc2\xa0a.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> August 8, before weakening back to a tropical storm at 12\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>.</p>\n<p>Bopha later made landfall on <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> at about 2\xc2\xa0a.m. local time on August 9. At this time, the JTWC reported that Bopha attained winds of 100\xc2\xa0km/h (65\xc2\xa0mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCBT10W_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCBT10W-36">[36]</a></sup> Tropical Storm Bopha then weakened into a tropical depression before degenerating into a remnant low on August 10.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">outer bands</a> of Tropical Storm Bopha produced heavy rains over northern <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, triggering flooding that destroyed 1,200 homes and killed seven people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Two of the fatalities occurred after a home was destroyed by a landslide in <a href="/wiki/Kalinga_(province)" title="Kalinga (province)">Kalinga Province</a>. The landslide damaged 20 other homes, a church and a school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As Severe Tropical Storm Bopha approached the island on August 8, the meteorological agency in Taiwan issued land and sea warnings for most of the region. Residents were warned about the possibility of torrential rains, flooding and mudslides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Although the storm was forecast to directly impact the island, all businesses remained open and schools were not closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In Hong Kong, the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> issued Standby Signal number one as Bopha came within 800\xc2\xa0km (500\xc2\xa0mi) of the city on August 9. This signal was later discontinued on August 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Between August 9 and 10, the remnants of Bopha produced moderate rainfall around Hong Kong, peaking at 45.6\xc2\xa0mm (1.80\xc2\xa0in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Wind gusts up to 110\xc2\xa0km/h (70\xc2\xa0mph) were also produced by the storm throughout the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> of 0.48\xc2\xa0m (1.6\xc2\xa0ft) was recorded in Tai Po Kau on August 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Wukong">Severe Tropical Storm Wukong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Wukong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Storm_Wukong_2006-08-16_lrg.jpg"><img alt="Tropical Storm Wukong 2006-08-16 lrg.jpg" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="7200" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Tropical_Storm_Wukong_2006-08-16_lrg.jpg/150px-Tropical_Storm_Wukong_2006-08-16_lrg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Tropical_Storm_Wukong_2006-08-16_lrg.jpg/225px-Tropical_Storm_Wukong_2006-08-16_lrg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Tropical_Storm_Wukong_2006-08-16_lrg.jpg/300px-Tropical_Storm_Wukong_2006-08-16_lrg.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wukong_2006_track.png"><img alt="Wukong 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1396" data-file-width="2000" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wukong_2006_track.png/150px-Wukong_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wukong_2006_track.png/225px-Wukong_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Wukong_2006_track.png/300px-Wukong_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 12\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 21</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>95\xc2\xa0km/h (60\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 980\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Wukong_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Wukong (2006)">Tropical Storm Wukong (2006)</a></div>\n<p>Tropical Depression 11W formed south of <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a> on August 12. Early on August 13, as it moved to the north-northwest, the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical storm. The JMA named it Wukong later that day. <a href="/wiki/Sun_Wukong" title="Sun Wukong">Wukong</a> was submitted by People\'s Republic of China, and it is the name of a character in a Chinese epic. Wukong absorbed Tropical Storm Sonamu shortly before landfall in Japan. Wukong then stalled over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ky%C5%ABsh%C5%AB" title="Ky\xc5\xabsh\xc5\xab">Ky\xc5\xabsh\xc5\xab</a>, before starting to jog to the north-northwest. It was downgraded to a tropical depression on August 20.</p>\n<p>In post-operational analysis by the JMA, Wukong was upgraded to a severe tropical storm.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Tropical_Storm_Sonamu_(Katring)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Sonamu_.28Katring.29">Tropical Storm Sonamu (Katring)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Sonamu (Katring)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Sonamu_2006.jpg"><img alt="TS Sonamu 2006.jpg" data-file-height="3555" data-file-width="2758" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/TS_Sonamu_2006.jpg/150px-TS_Sonamu_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/TS_Sonamu_2006.jpg/225px-TS_Sonamu_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/TS_Sonamu_2006.jpg/300px-TS_Sonamu_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sonamu_2006_track.png"><img alt="Sonamu 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Sonamu_2006_track.png/150px-Sonamu_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Sonamu_2006_track.png/225px-Sonamu_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Sonamu_2006_track.png/300px-Sonamu_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 13\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 16</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>65\xc2\xa0km/h (40\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 992\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On August 13, a tropical depression formed south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naha,_Okinawa" title="Naha, Okinawa">Naha, Okinawa</a>, and was named Katring by PAGASA and Sonamu by JMA. The name Sonamu was submitted by <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">DPR Korea</a> and signifies a <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine tree</a>. Sonamu began <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fujiwhara_interaction" title="Fujiwhara interaction">interacting</a> with nearby Tropical Storm Wukong on August 15, with the outflow from the stronger Wukong producing unfavourable shear over the cyclone. The JMA declared the system a tropical depression and stopped issuing advisories on August 16. The JTWC followed shortly after.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_13W">Tropical Depression 13W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 13W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2006_13W_NONAME_landfall.jpg"><img alt="2006 13W NONAME landfall.jpg" data-file-height="899" data-file-width="1024" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2006_13W_NONAME_landfall.jpg/150px-2006_13W_NONAME_landfall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2006_13W_NONAME_landfall.jpg/225px-2006_13W_NONAME_landfall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2006_13W_NONAME_landfall.jpg/300px-2006_13W_NONAME_landfall.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:13-W_2006_track.png"><img alt="13-W 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/13-W_2006_track.png/150px-13-W_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/13-W_2006_track.png/225px-13-W_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/13-W_2006_track.png/300px-13-W_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 22\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 25</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>55\xc2\xa0km/h (35\xc2\xa0mph)\xc2\xa0<small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In the afternoon of August 23, the <a href="/wiki/China_Meteorological_Administration" title="China Meteorological Administration">China Meteorological Administration</a> declared the formation of a tropical depression near <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> followed later that afternoon. The depression necessitated Tropical Cyclone Signal No.1 in Hong Kong and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, which means that the centre of a tropical cyclone is within 800\xc2\xa0km (500\xc2\xa0mi) of the respective <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Administrative_Region_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Special Administrative Region of the People\'s Republic of China">Special Administrative Regions</a>, and may later affect them. The depression made landfall at Guangdong at 5:55\xc2\xa0a.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Standard_Time" title="Chinese Standard Time">CST</a> on August 25 and dissipated later that morning.</p>\n<p>The JTWC designated the system as a Tropical Depression at 9\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> August 24, but only issued two warnings on the system.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Ioke">Typhoon Ioke</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Typhoon Ioke">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5\xc2\xa0super\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Ioke_Over_Wake_2006.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Ioke Over Wake 2006.jpg" data-file-height="9600" data-file-width="8000" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Typhoon_Ioke_Over_Wake_2006.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Ioke_Over_Wake_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Typhoon_Ioke_Over_Wake_2006.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Ioke_Over_Wake_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Typhoon_Ioke_Over_Wake_2006.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Ioke_Over_Wake_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ioke_2006_track.png"><img alt="Ioke 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1476" data-file-width="2000" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/150px-Ioke_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/225px-Ioke_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/300px-Ioke_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 27 <small>(<a href="/wiki/2006_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Ioke" title="2006 Pacific hurricane season">Entered basin</a>)</small>\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 6</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>195\xc2\xa0km/h (120\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 920\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a></div>\n<p>On August 27, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_storms_in_the_2006_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Ioke" title="List of storms in the 2006 Pacific hurricane season">Hurricane Ioke</a>, which had formed in the Central Pacific, crossed the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a> and entered the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a>\'s Area of Responsibility at around 6\xc2\xa0a.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>, keeping its name while being reclassified as Typhoon Ioke. Ioke had earlier affected <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Atoll" title="Johnston Atoll">Johnston Atoll</a>. On August 31 the center of the typhoon passed very close to <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a>; 200\xc2\xa0people were evacuated from there in advance of its approach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Typhoon Ioke then passed just to the northeast of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minami_Torishima" title="Minami Torishima">Minami Torishima</a>, which had been evacuated ahead of the storm, but as a weakened Category\xc2\xa03-equivalent typhoon. Ioke then turned to the northeast, weakening as it started undergoing extratropical transition. The JMA released its final advisory on September 7. The <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> remnants of Ioke moved into the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a> where it caused severe beach <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a> along the western Alaskan coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alaska_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alaska-46">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unnamed_Tropical_Storm">Unnamed Tropical Storm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Unnamed Tropical Storm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold;
