background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Possible_WPac_TS_September_6,_2006.jpg"><img alt="Possible WPac TS September 6, 2006.jpg" data-file-height="262" data-file-width="334" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Possible_WPac_TS_September_6%2C_2006.jpg/150px-Possible_WPac_TS_September_6%2C_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Possible_WPac_TS_September_6%2C_2006.jpg/225px-Possible_WPac_TS_September_6%2C_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Possible_WPac_TS_September_6%2C_2006.jpg/300px-Possible_WPac_TS_September_6%2C_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:September_2006_WPac_TS_track.png"><img alt="September 2006 WPac TS track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/September_2006_WPac_TS_track.png/150px-September_2006_WPac_TS_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/September_2006_WPac_TS_track.png/225px-September_2006_WPac_TS_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/September_2006_WPac_TS_track.png/300px-September_2006_WPac_TS_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 5\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 10</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>95\xc2\xa0km/h (60\xc2\xa0mph)\xc2\xa0<small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In early September, a tropical disturbance developed near Wake Island and gradually developed. Though never officially warned upon by any agency, meteorologist Gary Padgett and Dr. Karl Hoarau of <a href="/wiki/Cergy-Pontoise_University" title="Cergy-Pontoise University">Cergy-Pontoise University</a> surmised that the system likely was a tropical cyclone. Dr. Hoarau estimated that the system became a tropical depression early on September\xc2\xa05 and tracked north-northeast, attaining tropical storm intensity 18\xc2\xa0hours later. Around that time, the system featured a well-defined low-level circulation, significant convection wrapping around the circulation, and excellent <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a>. Additionally, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/QuikScat" title="QuikScat">QuikScat</a> pass revealed estimated surface winds of 95\xc2\xa0km/h (60\xc2\xa0mph). Around the time Dr. Haorau classified it a tropical storm, the JTWC issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> and their satellite intensity estimates reached T2.5, indicating a minimal tropical storm. On September\xc2\xa06, the system began to weaken as it turned north-northwest. Convection became intermittent, flaring around the circulation, and Dr. Haorau estimated it weakened to a depression later that day. Continuing northward, the system moved into a region of cooler waters and higher <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, inhibiting redevelopment. By September\xc2\xa09, the system became more <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> in nature and was last noted by the JTWC at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPsep_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPsep-47">[47]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Shanshan_(Luis)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Shanshan_.28Luis.29">Typhoon Shanshan (Luis)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Typhoon Shanshan (Luis)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg"><img alt="TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg" data-file-height="3972" data-file-width="3972" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg/150px-TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg/225px-TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg/300px-TyphoonShanshan-NRL16-9-06-modisvis250m.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shanshan_2006_track.png"><img alt="Shanshan 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1796" data-file-width="2000" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Shanshan_2006_track.png/150px-Shanshan_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Shanshan_2006_track.png/225px-Shanshan_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Shanshan_2006_track.png/300px-Shanshan_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 9\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 18</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>205\xc2\xa0km/h (125\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 919\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Shanshan_(2006)" title="Typhoon Shanshan (2006)">Typhoon Shanshan (2006)</a></div>\n<p>Hong Kong Observatory identified a tropical depression about 460\xc2\xa0kilometres north of Yap on September 9, the same day the JMA recognised it. The JTWC declared the formation of Tropical Depression 14W the next day. On the afternoon of September 10, it entered the PAGASA AOR and was named Luis. Later at 12\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> on the same day, the JMA upgraded the tropical depression to Tropical Storm Shanshan. The name Shanshan was contributed by Hong Kong and is a girls\' <a href="/wiki/Given_name" title="Given name">name</a>. Shanshan quickly strengthened and was upgraded into a severe tropical storm on September 11 and a typhoon later that day. Shanshan weakened slightly on September 14, but quickly restrengthened and reached Category\xc2\xa04 status on the JTWC\'s scale. Shanshan passed through the <a href="/wiki/Yaeyama_Islands" title="Yaeyama Islands">Yaeyama Islands</a> in the early morning hours of September 16. The JTWC reported that Shanshan was becoming <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> early on September 17, as the typhoon weakened to a tropical storm. The JTWC issued its final advisory on Shanshan later that day, and the JMA issued its last advisory on September 18, after Shanshan completed extratropical transition.</p>\n<p>As Shanshan neared <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Weather_Bureau" title="Central Weather Bureau">Central Weather Bureau</a> and local officials warned of flooding and high winds. However, as Shanshan turned towards Japan, all warnings were cancelled. South Korean forecasters also issued warnings ahead of an expected landfall, but this did not materialise. Ships were diverted as ports were closed as a precaution, while some other boats were forced to remain docked. In Japan, more than 90,000\xc2\xa0people were evacuated from <a href="/wiki/Yamaguchi_Prefecture" title="Yamaguchi Prefecture">Yamaguchi Prefecture</a>.</p>\n<p>Over 200\xc2\xa0people were injured by Shanshan and 11\xc2\xa0people were killed, mostly in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ky%C5%ABsh%C5%AB" title="Ky\xc5\xabsh\xc5\xab">Ky\xc5\xabsh\xc5\xab</a>, although two deaths were reported in South Korea. A tornado spawned by the typhoon caused a train derailment in <a href="/wiki/Nobeoka,_Miyazaki" title="Nobeoka, Miyazaki">Nobeoka, Miyazaki</a>, Japan which caused no fatalities. Peak gusts on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iriomote" title="Iriomote">Iriomote</a> reached 155\xc2\xa0mph (248\xc2\xa0km/h). Flights and trains were delayed, while electricity was cut to about 3000 homes in Korea. A ship also sank off <a href="/wiki/Ulleungdo" title="Ulleungdo">Ulleungdo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_15W">Tropical Depression 15W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 15W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:15W_2006_peak.jpg"><img alt="15W 2006 peak.jpg" data-file-height="899" data-file-width="1024" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/15W_2006_peak.jpg/150px-15W_2006_peak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/15W_2006_peak.jpg/225px-15W_2006_peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/15W_2006_peak.jpg/300px-15W_2006_peak.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:15-W_2006_track.png"><img alt="15-W 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/15-W_2006_track.png/150px-15-W_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/15-W_2006_track.png/225px-15-W_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/15-W_2006_track.png/300px-15-W_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 12\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 13</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>55\xc2\xa0km/h (35\xc2\xa0mph)\xc2\xa0<small>(1-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1004\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> identified a tropical depression about 360\xc2\xa0kilometres east-northeast of Xisha on September 12 and issued <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Tropical_Cyclone_Warning_Signals" title="Hong Kong Tropical Cyclone Warning Signals">Standby Signal No.1</a> accordingly. The tropical depression also necessitated the issuance of the Standby Signal No. 1 in Macau at 2\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> on the same day. The JTWC designated it as a tropical depression, 15W, at 9\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> September 12. The JMA had earlier already identified it as a tropical depression. As it strengthened and edged closer to the coastal areas of <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>, the Strong Wind Signal No. 3 was issued both in Hong Kong and Macau on September 13. It made landfall in western <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> around 11:30\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Standard_Time" title="Chinese Standard Time">CST</a> that night and dissipated inland.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Yagi">Typhoon Yagi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Typhoon Yagi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5\xc2\xa0super\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TyphoonYagi2006.jpg"><img alt="TyphoonYagi2006.jpg" data-file-height="3912" data-file-width="3496" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/TyphoonYagi2006.jpg/150px-TyphoonYagi2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/TyphoonYagi2006.jpg/225px-TyphoonYagi2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/TyphoonYagi2006.jpg/300px-TyphoonYagi2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yagi_2006_track.png"><img alt="Yagi 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1580" data-file-width="2000" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Yagi_2006_track.png/150px-Yagi_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Yagi_2006_track.png/225px-Yagi_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Yagi_2006_track.png/300px-Yagi_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 16\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 25</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>195\xc2\xa0km/h (120\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 910\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Yagi_(2006)" title="Typhoon Yagi (2006)">Typhoon Yagi (2006)</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> identified an area of disturbed weather northeast of <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">Chuuk</a> on September 13. The disturbance drifted to the north over the next few days, gradually increasing in organization. The JTWC issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> on the disturbance on September 16, and both the JTWC and JMA declared the system a tropical depression early on September 17. The JMA upgraded it to Tropical Storm Yagi later that morning as it moved erratically through the open Pacific Ocean, and the JTWC soon followed suit. The name Yagi was submitted by Japan and means <a href="/wiki/Capricornus" title="Capricornus">Capricornus</a> (goat). Yagi was upgraded to a severe tropical storm by the JMA on September 18, and the JTWC designated it a typhoon later that day. The JMA officially upgraded Yagi to typhoon status early on September 19. Yagi was upgraded briefly to a super typhoon by the JTWC from September 21 to 22. On September 23, the JTWC reported that Yagi was becoming <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> as it continued to weaken, and issued its final warning the next day. The JMA downgraded Yagi to a severe tropical storm on September 24. It was the third tropical cyclone in the NW Pacific Basin that attained Category\xc2\xa05 status in 2006. It started to recurve near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chichi-jima" title="Chichi-jima">Chichi-jima</a>, and never affected major land areas. It became <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> near the western <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutians</a> on September 25. Its extratropical remnants crossed the basin on September 27.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_17W">Tropical Depression 17W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression 17W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:17W_35_kt_2006-09-24_0530.jpg"><img alt="17W 35 kt 2006-09-24 0530.jpg" data-file-height="890" data-file-width="1024" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/17W_35_kt_2006-09-24_0530.jpg/150px-17W_35_kt_2006-09-24_0530.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/17W_35_kt_2006-09-24_0530.jpg/225px-17W_35_kt_2006-09-24_0530.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/17W_35_kt_2006-09-24_0530.jpg/300px-17W_35_kt_2006-09-24_0530.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:17-W_2006_track.png"><img alt="17-W 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/17-W_2006_track.png/150px-17-W_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/17-W_2006_track.png/225px-17-W_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/17-W_2006_track.png/300px-17-W_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 22\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 September 25</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>55\xc2\xa0km/h (35\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 996\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The China Meteorological Administration (CMA) and Hong Kong Observatory both identified a tropical depression in the southern <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> on September 22. The system was organized enough to be classified as Tropical Depression 17W by the JTWC the next day. It weakened under heavy vertical wind shear and the JTWC issued its final advisory on Tropical Depression 17W before landfall in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. The storm passed just south of Hainan and brought heavy rain to the area. The maximum rainfall recorded was 143\xc2\xa0mm. CMA kept it as a tropical storm until it made landfall in Vietnam in the morning of September 25.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Xangsane_(Milenyo)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Xangsane_.28Milenyo.29">Typhoon Xangsane (Milenyo)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Typhoon Xangsane (Milenyo)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Xangsane_27_sept_2006.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Xangsane 27 sept 2006.jpg" data-file-height="8000" data-file-width="6400" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Typhoon_Xangsane_27_sept_2006.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Xangsane_27_sept_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Typhoon_Xangsane_27_sept_2006.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Xangsane_27_sept_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Typhoon_Xangsane_27_sept_2006.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Xangsane_27_sept_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xangsane_2006_track.png"><img alt="Xangsane 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Xangsane_2006_track.png/150px-Xangsane_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Xangsane_2006_track.png/225px-Xangsane_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Xangsane_2006_track.png/300px-Xangsane_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 25\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>155\xc2\xa0km/h (100\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 940\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Xangsane" title="Typhoon Xangsane">Typhoon Xangsane</a></div>\n<p>On September 25, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> (PAGASA) named an active low pressure area within its area of responsibility Tropical Depression Milenyo. After issuing a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> earlier, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued its first warning on Tropical Depression 18W. On September 26 the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> named this system Xangsane. The name Xangsane was submitted by <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> and means elephant. Later that day, the JMA upgraded Xangsane to a severe tropical storm. A bout of rapid intensification followed, and all three agencies, the JMA, JTWC and PAGASA all upgraded the storm to a typhoon late on September 26 or early September 27. Xangsane made landfall on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samar_Island" title="Samar Island">Samar Island</a> as a severe tropical storm.</p>\n<p>The typhoon dropped heavy rainfall in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. To avoid the storm, transit authorities kept seacraft at several ports in the archipelago, leaving over 3,500 passengers stranded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Xangsane also prompted Philippine officials to close all schools, financial markets, and government offices in and around <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>. The typhoon killed over 200\xc2\xa0people in the country, and produced strong winds and rainfall, downing power lines and causing <a href="/wiki/Mudflow" title="Mudflow">mudflows</a>. The strong winds caused moderate crop damage totaling to $7.2\xc2\xa0million (2006\xc2\xa0USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Xangsane made landfall as a typhoon near <a href="/wiki/Hu%E1%BA%BF" title="Hu\xe1\xba\xbf">Hu\xe1\xba\xbf</a> early on October 1. The JTWC stopped issuing advisories soon after, and the JMA downgraded it to a severe tropical storm. Xangsane killed 71 in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Bebinca_(Neneng)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Severe_Tropical_Storm_Bebinca_.28Neneng.29">Severe Tropical Storm Bebinca (Neneng)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Bebinca (Neneng)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ccffff">Severe tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bebinca_Oct_5_2006_0415z.jpg"><img alt="Bebinca Oct 5 2006 0415z.jpg" data-file-height="7534" data-file-width="5738" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Bebinca_Oct_5_2006_0415z.jpg/150px-Bebinca_Oct_5_2006_0415z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Bebinca_Oct_5_2006_0415z.jpg/225px-Bebinca_Oct_5_2006_0415z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Bebinca_Oct_5_2006_0415z.jpg/300px-Bebinca_Oct_5_2006_0415z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bebinca_2006_track.png"><img alt="Bebinca 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1240" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Bebinca_2006_track.png/150px-Bebinca_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Bebinca_2006_track.png/225px-Bebinca_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Bebinca_2006_track.png/300px-Bebinca_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 28\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 6</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>95\xc2\xa0km/h (60\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 980\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On October 1, a persistent area of low pressure just east of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> developed into Tropical Depression 19W. The JMA had already been monitoring the storm. It was named Neneng by PAGASA, and later that evening was upgraded to a tropical storm by the Philippine authorities. The JMA and JTWC both designated the storm a tropical storm the next day, and it was named Bebinca by the JMA. Bebinca is a type of <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macanese</a> milk <a href="/wiki/Pudding" title="Pudding">pudding</a>.</p>\n<p>The JTWC downgraded it to a tropical depression briefly between October 4 and 5 as wind shear took its toll. Its low-level circulation then became exposed with dry air entering the system, and both the JMA and JTWC declared the storm as a dissipating tropical depression on October 6. It soon became entrained within the circulation of a storm-force <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical low</a>, which swept across the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honsh%C5%AB" title="Honsh\xc5\xab">Honsh\xc5\xab</a> coastal waters and led to 33\xc2\xa0people dead or missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> It was upgraded to a severe tropical storm in post analysis.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Rumbia">Tropical Storm Rumbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Rumbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rumbia_Oct_4_2006_0020z.jpg"><img alt="Rumbia Oct 4 2006 0020z.jpg" data-file-height="3995" data-file-width="3879" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rumbia_Oct_4_2006_0020z.jpg/150px-Rumbia_Oct_4_2006_0020z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rumbia_Oct_4_2006_0020z.jpg/225px-Rumbia_Oct_4_2006_0020z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rumbia_Oct_4_2006_0020z.jpg/300px-Rumbia_Oct_4_2006_0020z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rumbia_2006_track.png"><img alt="Rumbia 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Rumbia_2006_track.png/150px-Rumbia_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Rumbia_2006_track.png/225px-Rumbia_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Rumbia_2006_track.png/300px-Rumbia_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 3\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 6</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>85\xc2\xa0km/h (50\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 985\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On October 3, a tropical depression south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minami_Torishima" title="Minami Torishima">Minami Torishima</a> in high sea-surface temperatures gained enough convection and was designated Tropical Storm Rumbia by the JMA, although the JTWC had not even carried it as a tropical depression. Later that day, the JTWC issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a>, and began warnings on Tropical Depression 20W the next day. Rumbia slowly began to intensify while moving to the northwest, but on October 6 its low-level circulation became fully exposed, and the JTWC issued a final warning. The JMA followed suit soon after. The remnants of Rumbia later became extremely elongated on October 6, before being absorbed into the large extratropical low of Bebinca. The name "<i>Rumbia</i>" comes from a type of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_tree" title="Palm tree">palm tree</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Sago" title="Sago">sago</a> palm.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Soulik">Typhoon Soulik</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Typhoon Soulik">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soulik_14_Oct_06_02Z.jpg"><img alt="Soulik 14 Oct 06 02Z.jpg" data-file-height="889" data-file-width="1024" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soulik_14_Oct_06_02Z.jpg/150px-Soulik_14_Oct_06_02Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soulik_14_Oct_06_02Z.jpg/225px-Soulik_14_Oct_06_02Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soulik_14_Oct_06_02Z.jpg/300px-Soulik_14_Oct_06_02Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soulik_2006_track.png"><img alt="Soulik 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1556" data-file-width="2000" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Soulik_2006_track.png/150px-Soulik_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Soulik_2006_track.png/225px-Soulik_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Soulik_2006_track.png/300px-Soulik_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 8\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 16</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>140\xc2\xa0km/h (85\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 955\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On October\xc2\xa06, a tropical disturbance formed about 240\xc2\xa0km (150\xc2\xa0mi) north-northeast of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kwajalein" title="Kwajalein">Kwajalein</a> with <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">convection</a> nearby, developing a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a> two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Summary_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Summary-11">[11]</a></sup> On October\xc2\xa08, the JMA began monitoring the system as a tropical depression, upgrading it to Tropical Storm Soulik the next day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMAATCR_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMAATCR-52">[52]</a></sup> while the JTWC classified it as Tropical Depression 21W.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCBT006_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCBT006-53">[53]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anticyclone</a> to the north and a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_upper_tropospheric_trough" title="Tropical upper tropospheric trough">tropical upper tropospheric trough</a> cell to the west provided <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> for the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Summary_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Summary-11">[11]</a></sup> Soulik tracked northwestward around a <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a>, slowly intensifying due to <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Summary_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Summary-11">[11]</a></sup> Around 1200\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on October\xc2\xa010, the JTWC upgraded Soulik to a typhoon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCBT006_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCBT006-53">[53]</a></sup> and the JMA followed suit late on October\xc2\xa012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMAATCR_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-JMAATCR-52">[52]</a></sup> Another ridge west of Soulik turned the storm northward, and the influence of both ridges caused Soulik to become nearly stationary about 100\xc2\xa0km (65\xc2\xa0mi) south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Summary_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Summary-11">[11]</a></sup> According to the JTWC, Soulik attained 1\xc2\xa0minute winds of 165\xc2\xa0km/h (105\xc2\xa0mph)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWCBT006_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-JTWCBT006-53">[53]</a></sup> while the JMA reported 10\xc2\xa0minute winds of 140\xc2\xa0km/h (85\xc2\xa0mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMAATCR_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-JMAATCR-52">[52]</a></sup> At 0600\xc2\xa0UTC on October\xc2\xa014, Soulik passed within 40\xc2\xa0km (25\xc2\xa0mi) of Iwo Jima. According to the JTWC, this would place the island within an area affected by typhoon-force winds. Later that day, an approaching <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a> increased the wind shear, causing the typhoon to weaken. By 1200\xc2\xa0UTC on October\xc2\xa016, Soulik had transitioned into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> as it rapidly traveled towards the northeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Summary_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Summary-11">[11]</a></sup> The remnants were last noted south of the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> on October\xc2\xa017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMAATCR_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-JMAATCR-52">[52]</a></sup></p>\n<p>At 0600\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on October\xc2\xa09, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical storm watch</a> was issued for <a href="/wiki/Agrihan" title="Agrihan">Agrihan</a> in the northern <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unisys1_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Unisys1-54">[54]</a></sup> upgraded to a warning the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unisys2_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Unisys2-55">[55]</a></sup> During the storm\'s passage, a total of 206\xc2\xa0mm (8.11\xc2\xa0in) of rain was recorded on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pagan_Island" title="Pagan Island">Pagan Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unisys5_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Unisys5-56">[56]</a></sup> Sustained winds on the island reached 58\xc2\xa0km/h (36\xc2\xa0mph) and gusts reached 122\xc2\xa0km/h (76\xc2\xa0mph), although there was no damage in the region<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCDC_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCDC-57">[57]</a></sup> Waves up to 7.6\xc2\xa0m (25\xc2\xa0ft) affected the <a href="/wiki/Bonin_Islands" title="Bonin Islands">Bonin Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMX2_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMX2-58">[58]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Iwo_Jima" title="Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a>, winds were recorded up to 160\xc2\xa0km/h (100\xc2\xa0mph) with gusts up to 210\xc2\xa0km/h (130\xc2\xa0mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMX1_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMX1-59">[59]</a></sup> Although Soulik spent over a day near Iwo Jima, no damage was reported as a result of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Ompong">Tropical Depression Ompong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Ompong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(PAGASA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ompong_2006_cropped.jpg"><img alt="Ompong 2006 cropped.jpg" data-file-height="2701" data-file-width="2442" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ompong_2006_cropped.jpg/150px-Ompong_2006_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ompong_2006_cropped.jpg/225px-Ompong_2006_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ompong_2006_cropped.jpg/300px-Ompong_2006_cropped.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ompong_(PAGASA)_2006_track.png"><img alt="Ompong (PAGASA) 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ompong_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png/150px-Ompong_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ompong_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png/225px-Ompong_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ompong_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png/300px-Ompong_%28PAGASA%29_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 12\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 October 13</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>55\xc2\xa0km/h (35\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On October 12, a tropical disturbance that had been meandering in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Area of Responsibility</a> was designated Tropical Depression Ompong by PAGASA. The depression slowly moved westward toward the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, but wind shear from Typhoon Soulik prevented any intensification. The depression degenerated into an area of low pressure early the next day.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Cimaron_(Paeng)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Cimaron_.28Paeng.29">Typhoon Cimaron (Paeng)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Typhoon Cimaron (Paeng)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5\xc2\xa0super\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TY_Cimaron_2006_peak.jpg"><img alt="TY Cimaron 2006 peak.jpg" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="6000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/TY_Cimaron_2006_peak.jpg/150px-TY_Cimaron_2006_peak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/TY_Cimaron_2006_peak.jpg/225px-TY_Cimaron_2006_peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/TY_Cimaron_2006_peak.jpg/300px-TY_Cimaron_2006_peak.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cimaron_2006_track.png"><img alt="Cimaron 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Cimaron_2006_track.png/150px-Cimaron_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Cimaron_2006_track.png/225px-Cimaron_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Cimaron_2006_track.png/300px-Cimaron_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 25\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 November 6</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>185\xc2\xa0km/h (115\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 920\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Cimaron_(2006)" title="Typhoon Cimaron (2006)">Typhoon Cimaron (2006)</a></div>\n<p>An area of disturbed weather developed northwest of <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">Chuuk</a> on October 24. The disturbance moved west-northwestward over the next two days and gradually became better organized, and the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> on the system on October 26. The system was designated Tropical Depression 22W by the JTWC later that day. The system continued to strengthen, and the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical storm on October 27. The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> later followed suit and designated the system Tropical Storm Cimaron. The name Cimaron was submitted by the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, and is a type of wild <a href="/wiki/Ox" title="Ox">ox</a>. The system quickly intensified, and was upgraded to a severe tropical storm by the JMA later that day. The system continued its quick intensification and was upgraded to a typhoon by both the JTWC and JMA on October 28. Further intensification occurred overnight, and the typhoon had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapidly deepened</a> 65 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> in 24 hours, from 985\xc2\xa0hPa to 920\xc2\xa0hPa, causing the JTWC to upgrade it to a 140-kn super typhoon at 9\xc2\xa0a.m. UTC on October 29. It made landfall at about 12:30\xc2\xa0p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a> the same day on Northern <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>. There, especially in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabela_Province" title="Isabela Province">Isabela Province</a>, it lashed winds as much as 195\xc2\xa0km/h and gusts as much as 230\xc2\xa0km/h.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Actually, all or parts of four provinces (Isabela, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quirino_Province" title="Quirino Province">Quirino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cagayan" title="Cagayan">Cagayan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aurora_Province" title="Aurora Province">Aurora</a>) are declared under Signal No. 4 as the typhoon struck the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Cimaron then re-intensified after crossing the island, but not to its original strength, and was expected to curve towards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hainan_Island" title="Hainan Island">Hainan</a>, instead of moving towards <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> as previously forecast. On November 1, the JTWC upgraded the typhoon back into a Category\xc2\xa03-equivalent storm, and forecast that it would make a direct impact on Hong Kong. However, prediction models showed conflicting forecasts, and Cimaron remained quasi-stationary and weakened to a severe tropical storm on November 2. Dry air entrainment caused further weakening, with the JTWC dropping it to a minimal tropical storm at 3\xc2\xa0p.m. UTC the next day. It weakened further, upwelling itself. The JTWC issued its final warning at 3\xc2\xa0p.m. UTC on November 4. The JMA continued advisories on Cimaron until 12\xc2\xa0a.m. UTC on November 6, when it was downgraded to a weak tropical depression.</p>\n<p>The typhoon killed at least 19\xc2\xa0people, many of whom drowned, and left 15 missing in the northern Philippines. It also killed a woman and her child after both are hit by a sheet of galvanized iron in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dilasag" title="Dilasag">Dilasag</a>, Aurora Province, serving as the first human casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Further casualties happened as the typhoon passed through Luzon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Despite these, however, classes in <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">Metro Manila</a> were still not suspended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> It also caused at least US$9\xc2\xa0million in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> 90% of the houses were damaged in a coastal town near where Cimaron made landfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In the aftermath of the storm\'s passage across the Philippines, the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_International_Development_Cooperation_Agency" title="Swedish International Development Cooperation Agency">Swedish International Development Cooperation Agency</a> contributed 2.5\xc2\xa0million <a href="/wiki/Swedish_krona" title="Swedish krona">Swedish krona</a> (US$350,000) to aid efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Chebi_(Queenie)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Chebi_.28Queenie.29">Typhoon Chebi (Queenie)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Typhoon Chebi (Queenie)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Chebi_2006.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Chebi 2006.jpg" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="542" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Typhoon_Chebi_2006.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Chebi_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Typhoon_Chebi_2006.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Chebi_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Typhoon_Chebi_2006.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Chebi_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chebi_2006_track.png"><img alt="Chebi 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Chebi_2006_track.png/150px-Chebi_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Chebi_2006_track.png/225px-Chebi_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Chebi_2006_track.png/300px-Chebi_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>November 8\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 November 14</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>185\xc2\xa0km/h (115\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 925\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chebi" title="Typhoon Chebi">Typhoon Chebi</a></div>\n<p>An area of disturbed weather developed east of the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a> on October 31, and moved west-northwestward over the next week without any increase in organization due to an unfavorable environment, until November 6, when it encountered more favorable conditions, and the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> declared it a tropical depression on November 8. The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> on the system later that day, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> named the system Tropical Depression Queenie shortly after. The JTWC classified it as Tropical Depression 23W early on November 9. According to the JTWC, lack of equatorial outflow prevented rapid intensification of the system. Later that day at 12\xc2\xa0p.m. UTC, the JMA upgraded it to a tropical storm named it Chebi. The name Jebi, the correct spelling means <a href="/wiki/Swallow" title="Swallow">swallow</a> in Korean. The JTWC and PAGASA both followed suit later that day. Early on November 10, the JMA upgraded Chebi to a severe tropical storm as it continued to move west towards the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, following a similar track as Typhoon Cimaron earlier in the season.</p>\n<p>Just hours later, the JMA upgraded Chebi from severe tropical storm with 10-minute sustained winds of 55\xc2\xa0knots to a typhoon with winds of 95\xc2\xa0knots, with a pressure decrease of 40 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> over three hours. The JTWC followed suit, upping Chebi from a tropical storm with 1-minute sustained winds of 55\xc2\xa0knots to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 4-equivalent</a> typhoon at 9\xc2\xa0a.m. UTC. PAGASA raised Public Storm Warning Signal No. 4 for three provinces in <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, making Chebi the second storm (Typhoon Cimaron served as the first one that year.) in as many weeks to force a Signal #4. After <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapidly deepening</a>, Chebi weakened as it approached the Philippines. It made its first landfall near <a href="/wiki/Casiguran,_Aurora" title="Casiguran, Aurora">Casiguran, Aurora</a> early on November 11, crossed the <a href="/wiki/Lingayen_Gulf" title="Lingayen Gulf">Lingayen Gulf</a> and its second landfall on <a href="/wiki/Barangay" title="Barangay">Barangay</a> Lucap, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaminos_City" title="Alaminos City">Alaminos City</a> about 8 hours later.</p>\n<p>Encountering dry air entrainment and increased vertical <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, Chebi began to gradually weaken to a severe tropical storm on November 12. It continued to weaken, turning northwards towards <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a>, and was downgraded to a tropical storm the next day. On November 14, the JMA issued its last advisory on the dissipating tropical depression. The JTWC issued its final warning later that same day as Chebi dissipated under the strong shear.</p>\n<p>All told, the typhoon caused further casualties as well as damage caused by the earlier Typhoon Cimaron. After passing through Luzon, it left 1 dead and 10 injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aurora_Province" title="Aurora Province">Aurora Province</a>, it caused floods, cutting the province\'s road system,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> as well as zero visibility, further isolating it from relief efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Durian_(Reming)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Durian_.28Reming.29">Typhoon Durian (Reming)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Typhoon Durian (Reming)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4\xc2\xa0super\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Durian_2006-11-29_0730Z.png"><img alt="Durian 2006-11-29 0730Z.png" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1920" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Durian_2006-11-29_0730Z.png/150px-Durian_2006-11-29_0730Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Durian_2006-11-29_0730Z.png/225px-Durian_2006-11-29_0730Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Durian_2006-11-29_0730Z.png/300px-Durian_2006-11-29_0730Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Durian_2006_track.png"><img alt="Durian 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Durian_2006_track.png/150px-Durian_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Durian_2006_track.png/225px-Durian_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Durian_2006_track.png/300px-Durian_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>November 25\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 December 6 <small>(<a href="/wiki/2006_North_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season#Tropical_Depression_Durian" title="2006 North Indian Ocean cyclone season">Exited basin</a>)</small></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>195\xc2\xa0km/h (120\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 915\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Durian" title="Typhoon Durian">Typhoon Durian</a></div>\n<p>An area of disturbed weather developed southeast of <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">Chuuk</a> on November 24. <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">Wind shear</a> near the disturbance soon decreased, allowing the depression to organize a little. It was designated a tropical depression by <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> on November 25, and later that day the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> started issuing warnings on the system as it moved west-northwest towards <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">Yap</a>. The depression strengthened because it was in an area of high sea-surface temperatures, and there were distinct cloud features of <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anticyclonic</a> outflow, according to the JMA. It was upgraded to a tropical storm on the afternoon of November 26 and named Durian. The name Durian refers to a fruit, "<a href="/wiki/Durian" title="Durian">Durio zibethinus</a>", and was submitted to the naming list by <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.</p>\n<p>Moving west to west-northwestward, Durian intensified slowly. It became a severe tropical storm on November 27, and the next day it was named <i>Reming</i> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> when it entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility. Later on November 28, both the JMA and JTWC upgraded it to a typhoon as it continued to track towards the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. A quick bout of intensification occurred on November 29, causing the JMA to upgrade the storm to 100\xc2\xa0knots in wind intensity, and the JTWC to give it a <a href="/wiki/Dvorak_technique" title="Dvorak technique">Dvorak classification</a> of 6.5 (127\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">kn</a>) in a <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> fix. In 6 hours, Durian intensified from 90 kn 1-minute sustained winds to 125\xc2\xa0kn winds. The JTWC then forecast a direct hit over <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">Metro Manila</a> later that day when it upgraded the storm to a super typhoon. PAGASA raised Public Storm Warning Signal 4, its highest warning level, over <a href="/wiki/Catanduanes" title="Catanduanes">Catanduanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albay" title="Albay">Albay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camarines_Norte" title="Camarines Norte">Camarines Norte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camarines_Sur" title="Camarines Sur">Camarines Sur</a>. It was the third time in 2006, and the third time in a row, that PAGASA raised Signal #4. Durian began to weaken slightly as it approached land, undergoing an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a>, but quickly regained peak strength.</p>\n<p>PAGASA claimed that the storm made landfall on the morning of November 30 over southern <a href="/wiki/Catanduanes" title="Catanduanes">Catanduanes</a>, although the JMA and JTWC did not recognize this landfall. Durian then made another landfall after crossing the <a href="/wiki/Lagonoy_Gulf" title="Lagonoy Gulf">Lagonoy Gulf</a> in northeastern <a href="/wiki/Albay" title="Albay">Albay</a>. After weakening due to interaction with land, Durian was downgraded back to a typhoon by the JTWC. The storm continued to move west, making landfalls on the <a href="/wiki/Bondoc_Peninsula" title="Bondoc Peninsula">Bondoc Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quezon" title="Quezon">Quezon</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Marinduque" title="Marinduque">Marinduque</a> and finally on <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Mindoro" title="Oriental Mindoro">Oriental Mindoro</a> before exiting to the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>.</p>\n<p>Encountering dry air entrainment and vertical <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, Durian weakened slightly at first, but slowly began to reorganise and restrengthen as it neared <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. Durian began to turn slightly southwest towards <a href="/wiki/Nha_Trang" title="Nha Trang">Nha Trang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Ho Chi Minh City</a> on December 3. Eventually, Durian began to weaken again, and by December 4, the JMA downgraded it to a severe tropical storm. The storm maintained intensity as it skirted the Vietnamese coast moving southwest. After a brief second stint at typhoon strength, Durian finally made landfall in <a href="/wiki/B%E1%BA%BFn_Tre_Province" title="B\xe1\xba\xbfn Tre Province">B\xe1\xba\xbfn Tre Province</a> on December 5. The system rapidly weakened over land, and the JMA downgraded it to a tropical storm. The JMA and JTWC issued their final advisories later that day as Durian emerged into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a> as a weak tropical depression. The remnants of Durian then crossed the coast of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Thailand" title="Southern Thailand">southern Thailand</a> as it moved into the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>.</p>\n<p>The storm killed at least 720 in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The most damage occurred in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albay_Province" title="Albay Province">Albay Province</a> where the storm created mudslides of volcanic ash and boulders off <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayon_Volcano" title="Mayon Volcano">Mayon Volcano</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The Padang <a href="/wiki/Barangay" title="Barangay">barangay</a> of <a href="/wiki/Legazpi,_Albay" title="Legazpi, Albay">Legazpi City</a> was severely affected with a large portion of the town covered in mud up to houses\' roofs. At least 81\xc2\xa0people have died and 16\xc2\xa0people are missing in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> from the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Typhoon_Utor_(Seniang)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Typhoon_Utor_.28Seniang.29">Typhoon Utor (Seniang)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Typhoon Utor (Seniang)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #fdaf9a">Typhoon\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3\xc2\xa0typhoon\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Utor_13_dec_2006_0305Z.jpg"><img alt="Typhoon Utor 13 dec 2006 0305Z.jpg" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="6400" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Typhoon_Utor_13_dec_2006_0305Z.jpg/150px-Typhoon_Utor_13_dec_2006_0305Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Typhoon_Utor_13_dec_2006_0305Z.jpg/225px-Typhoon_Utor_13_dec_2006_0305Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Typhoon_Utor_13_dec_2006_0305Z.jpg/300px-Typhoon_Utor_13_dec_2006_0305Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Utor_2006_track.png"><img alt="Utor 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Utor_2006_track.png/150px-Utor_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Utor_2006_track.png/225px-Utor_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Utor_2006_track.png/300px-Utor_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>December 7\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 December 15</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>155\xc2\xa0km/h (100\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 945\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Utor_(2006)" title="Typhoon Utor (2006)">Typhoon Utor (2006)</a></div>\n<p>On December 2, an area of convection was spotted by the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> southeast of <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">Chuuk</a>. Although convection decreased in the next few hours, on December 5 the JTWC once again noted flaring deep convection, and late on December 6 a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a> was issued. On the morning of December 7, both the JTWC and <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a>-RSMC Tokyo reported that a tropical depression had formed. Soon after, the depression entered the area of responsibility of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a>, who named it Seniang. The depression strengthened throughout the day, and the JMA upgraded it to Tropical Storm Utor later that day. The name Utor was submitted by the United States on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, and is a <a href="/wiki/Marshallese_language" title="Marshallese language">Marshallese</a> word for <a href="/wiki/Squall_line" title="Squall line">squall line</a>.Signal no.3 has been raised in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a>,Leyte,Samar Provinces</p>\n<p>On December 8, the JMA upgraded Utor to a severe tropical storm. It intensified further and was upgraded to a typhoon by the JMA on the morning of December 9, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> and JTWC doing the same. The storm made landfall shortly after noon local time the same day. After crossing the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, Utor took a track similar to Typhoon Chebi in November, first moving northwest then threatening to take aim at Hong Kong. It restrengthened to an 85-kn typhoon, before it slowed as it tracked in a weak steering environment within a weakness in the <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a>. It then weakened as wind shear increased and dry air entrainment occurred. The JMA downgraded it to a severe tropical storm on December 13, and to a tropical storm the same day. The next day the JTWC downgraded the storm to a tropical storm and issued its last advisory.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Summit" title="ASEAN Summit">2006 ASEAN</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>, originally scheduled to start December 10, was put back a month due to the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Typhoon Utor killed at least 78 people and left 49 others missing in the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Damages from the typhoon were estimated at $1.9\xc2\xa0million (2006 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Typhoon Utor was blamed for heavy rains of up to 350\xc2\xa0mm within 24 hours in southern <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia" title="Peninsular Malaysia">Peninsular Malaysia</a>, specifically <a href="/wiki/Johor" title="Johor">Johor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Negeri_Sembilan" title="Negeri Sembilan">Negeri Sembilan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melaka" title="Melaka">Melaka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pahang" title="Pahang">Pahang</a>, causing massive floods within the southern region on December 18, 2006, which was considered as the worst in the <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysian</a> southern region history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Segamat-flood01_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Segamat-flood01-79">[79]</a></sup> However, there were also reports a few days earlier that adverse weather was not to be blamed on the typhoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The worst-affected areas were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Segamat" title="Segamat">Segamat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kota_Tinggi" title="Kota Tinggi">Kota Tinggi</a>, where both towns were totally inaccessible by land after all main roads leading to those towns were all flooded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Segamat-flood02_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Segamat-flood02-81">[81]</a></sup> Until December 24, 2006, the floods had claimed 8 lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Segamat-flood03_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Segamat-flood03-82">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Tropical_Storm_Trami_(Tomas)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Trami_.28Tomas.29">Tropical Storm Trami (Tomas)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Trami (Tomas)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(JMA)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trami_2006.jpg"><img alt="Trami 2006.jpg" data-file-height="3285" data-file-width="3067" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Trami_2006.jpg/150px-Trami_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Trami_2006.jpg/225px-Trami_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Trami_2006.jpg/300px-Trami_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0</span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trami_2006_track.png"><img alt="Trami 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="2000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Trami_2006_track.png/150px-Trami_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Trami_2006_track.png/225px-Trami_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Trami_2006_track.png/300px-Trami_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>December 15\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 December 20</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>65\xc2\xa0km/h (40\xc2\xa0mph) <small>(10-min)</small>\xc2\xa0 1000\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>\xc2\xa0(<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On December 16, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> started issuing public bulletins on a tropical depression southwest of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> initiated warnings on Tropical Depression 26W the next day, despite having not issued a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert" title="Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert">Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert</a>. The system was upgraded to a tropical storm by the JMA and named Trami, which is a kind of <a href="/wiki/Rose" title="Rose">rose</a> tree. This name was submitted by <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. The storm moved west-northwest rapidly towards the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, but struggled against wind shear and an approaching cold front. Entering the PAGASA Area of Responsibility on December 18 as it maintained minimal tropical storm intensity, it was named Tomas. The JTWC issued its final warning later that day, having never upgraded the storm to tropical storm strength, citing no indication of a significant low-level circulation centre. On December 19, the JMA downgraded the storm to a tropical depression and issued its last public bulletin as the storm dissipated over water.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_systems">Other systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Other systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On March 7, the JMA had upgraded a low-pressure area to a tropical depression formed by the remnants of 01W to the southeast of <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> During the next day, the system moved overland and made landfall over in <a href="/wiki/Davao_City" title="Davao City">Davao</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The system emerged to the <a href="/wiki/Sulu_Sea" title="Sulu Sea">Sulu Sea</a>, nearing <a href="/wiki/Palawan" title="Palawan">Palawan</a> until it weakened back into a low-pressure are on March 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> On March 11, the same system emerged to the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> as the JMA had re-upgraded it back to a tropical depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Although the system had experienced shear and became an exposed system, the depression fully dissipated late on March 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On July 3, both the China Meteorological Administration (CMA) and the JMA had identified a tropical depression about 200\xc2\xa0km south of <a href="/wiki/Sanya" title="Sanya">Sanya</a>, Hainan. The depression moved northwest and made landfall a in Hainan on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The depression made its second landfall over in the border of northern <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> as it rapidly deteriorated and absorbed by a front on July 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Early on July 21, the CMA classified it as a tropical depression.
