The CMA issued its final warning on July 22 as it started to weaken rapidly. The system was absorbed by Typhoon Kaemi and fully dissipated on July 25. The JMA only classified the system as a low-pressure area throughout its lifetime. On July 28, a tropical depression had rapidly organized and persisted over in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tonkin" title="Gulf of Tonkin">Gulf of Tonkin</a> and made landfall in the same location as the previous system at its peak strength with a pressure of 998 mbar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The system moved over land and fully dissipated on July 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On September 13, two tropical depressions were monitored by the JMA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09.2F13.2F06_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-09.2F13.2F06-92">[92]</a></sup> The first one persisted just south of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and dissipated later on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-09.2F13.2F06_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-09.2F13.2F06-92">[92]</a></sup> The second system formed from a <a href="/wiki/Stationary_front" title="Stationary front">stationary front</a> near <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and moved northwards. By September 15, the system dissipated while making landfall over in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A trio of tropical depressions were also monitored by the JMA during late October. The first developed on October 21 about north of the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The depression moved stationary until its circulation became exposed due to shear on October 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The other two systems were also monitored very briefly by the JMA during October 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.2F22.2F06_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-10.2F22.2F06-96">[96]</a></sup> One in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> as it moved westwards and fully dissipated six hours later, where its remnants made landfall in Vietnam during the next day; whilst the other persisted over in the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">Philippine Sea</a> also bringing rainfall to <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a> during October 25, just before the arrival of Typhoon Cimaron.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.2F22.2F06_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-10.2F22.2F06-96">[96]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a></div>\n<p>Within the North-western Pacific Ocean, both the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> assign names to tropical cyclones that develop in the Western Pacific, which can result in a tropical cyclone having two names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_Dec_99_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-97">[97]</a></sup> The Japan Meteorological Agency\'s RSMC Tokyo\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 Typhoon Center assigns international names to tropical cyclones on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>\'s Typhoon Committee, should they be judged to have 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 65\xc2\xa0km/h, (40\xc2\xa0mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-TC-98">[98]</a></sup> While the Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration assigns names to tropical cyclones which move into or form as a tropical depression in their area of responsibility located between 135\xc2\xb0E and 115\xc2\xb0E and between 5\xc2\xb0N-25\xc2\xb0N even if the cyclone has had an international name assigned to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_Dec_99_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-97">[97]</a></sup> The names of significant tropical cyclones are retired, by both <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Philippine_typhoon_names" title="List of retired Philippine typhoon names">PAGASA</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names_(JMA)" title="List of retired Pacific typhoon names (JMA)">Typhoon Committee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-TC-98">[98]</a></sup> Should the list of names for the Philippine region be exhausted then names will be taken from an auxiliary list of which the first ten are published each season. Unused names are marked in <span style="color:#666666">gray</span>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_names">International names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: International names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names" title="List of retired Pacific typhoon names">List of retired Pacific typhoon names</a></div>\n<p>During the season 22 tropical storms developed in the Western Pacific and each one was named by the JMA, when the system was judged to have 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 65\xc2\xa0km/h (40\xc2\xa0mph). The JMA selected the names from a list of 140 names, that had been developed by the 14 members nations and territories of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names#Background" title="List of retired Pacific typhoon names">ESCAP/WMO Typhoon Committee</a>. After the season the Typhoon Committee retired the names Chanchu, Bilis, Saomai, Xangsane and Durian. They were replaced with Sanba, Maliksi, Son-Tinh, Leepi and Mangkhut, respectively.</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tr>\n<td>Chanchu</td>\n<td>Jelawat</td>\n<td>Ewiniar</td>\n<td>Bilis</td>\n<td>Kaemi</td>\n<td>Prapiroon</td>\n<td>Maria</td>\n<td>Saomai</td>\n<td>Bopha</td>\n<td>Wukong</td>\n<td>Sonamu</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Shanshan</td>\n<td>Yagi</td>\n<td>Xangsane</td>\n<td>Bebinca</td>\n<td>Rumbia</td>\n<td>Soulik</td>\n<td>Cimaron</td>\n<td>Chebi</td>\n<td>Durian</td>\n<td>Utor</td>\n<td>Trami</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right;">\n<tr>\n<td>Agaton</td>\n<td>Basyang</td>\n<td>Caloy</td>\n<td>Domeng</td>\n<td>Ester</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Florita</td>\n<td>Glenda</td>\n<td>Henry</td>\n<td>Inday</td>\n<td>Juan</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Katring</td>\n<td>Luis</td>\n<td>Milenyo</td>\n<td>Neneng</td>\n<td>Ompong</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Paeng</td>\n<td>Queenie</td>\n<td>Reming</td>\n<td>Seniang</td>\n<td>Tomas</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Usman\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Venus\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Waldo\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Yayang\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Zeny\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="5">Auxiliary list</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Agila\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Bagwis\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Chito\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Diego\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Elena\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Felino\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Gunding\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Harriet\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Indang\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n<td><span style="color:#666666">Jessa\xc2\xa0<i>(unused)</i></span></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>During the season PAGASA used its own naming scheme for the 19 tropical cyclones, that either developed within or moved into their self-defined area of responsibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pagasa_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-pagasa-99">[99]</a></sup> The names were taken from a list of names, that had been last used during <a href="/wiki/2002_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2002 Pacific typhoon season">2002</a> and was scheduled to be used again during <a href="/wiki/2010_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2010 Pacific typhoon season">2010</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pagasa_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-pagasa-99">[99]</a></sup> Many names were used for the first time as PAGASA had revised their naming lists during 2003. Although the name <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chataan" title="Typhoon Chataan">Gloria</a> from 2002 was retired and replaced with Glenda, as it was the name of the <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo" title="Gloria Macapagal Arroyo">incumbent Philippine president</a> at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pagasa_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-pagasa-99">[99]</a></sup></p>\n<p>After the season, PAGASA had stated that the names Milenyo and Reming will be retired as they had caused over <a href="/wiki/Philippine_peso" title="Philippine peso">Php</a>1 billion in damages and over 300 fatalities. They were subsequently replaced on the list with <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Fung-wong_(2014)" title="Tropical Storm Fung-wong (2014)">Mario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Hagupit_(2014)" title="Typhoon Hagupit (2014)">Ruby</a>. Both names, however, were retired after the 2014 season, being replaced by Maymay and Rosita respectively.</p>\n<p><br/></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_typhoon_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This table summarizes all the systems that developed within or moved into the North Pacific Ocean, to the west of the International Date Line during 2006. The tables also provide an overview of a systems intensity, duration, land areas affected and any deaths or damages associated with the system.</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders"
